Diplomatic Support Association

Request Further Negotiations on the Dutch Tax Increase Case 122

Strive to achieve the goal of withdrawing the original plan. The China-Dutch Diplomatic Support Association believes that the Dutch increase in immigration tax of 150 guilders per person will cause China to lose 20 million yuan annually, and the impact is beyond calculation. Therefore, yesterday, it sent telegrams to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs and the Acting Agent Dai stationed in the Netherlands requesting continued negotiations. The telegram texts are recorded as follows: (A) Telegram to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs in Nanjing: We have investigated the case of the Dutch colonial council's decision to increase the immigration tax to 150 guilders per person. Overseas Chinese groups and enthusiastic overseas Chinese have repeatedly called for negotiations. Fortunately, your ministry adopted the protest of the Acting Agent Dai stationed in the Netherlands, which has been repeatedly postponed. However, the association believes that if this case is not fundamentally revoked, the ashes will eventually rekindle. Therefore, on February 8th, it sent a telegram requesting continued negotiations, but there was no late indication of profoundness. I originally wanted to "shut up" to avoid offending the public. However, bad news came and the situation changed again. The Dutch government saw that our government no longer protested, the public no longer opposed the Dutch, Dutch ships were sailing as usual, and Dutch sugar was still being transported to China. Since diplomacy was no longer worried, the tax increase would be implemented, and they would even make further progress and set other penalties of hundreds of guilders. Your ministry's efforts are in vain, and the people will suffer. The association is sincerely grieved and humbly requests your ministry to uphold the spirit of loving overseas Chinese and take a firm attitude to send telegrams to all parties to continue protesting. The protest will not end until the case is revoked to maintain the survival of all overseas Chinese in the Netherlands, recover the annual loss of 20 million yuan, and bring honor to the party and the country and benefit the people. The association has no selfish interests. Finally, I humbly request you to accept my final plea. China-Dutch Diplomatic Support Association (B) Telegram to Agent Dai in The Hague, Chinese Embassy in The Hague, Agent Dai: I have repeatedly read the documents of your protest against the Dutch increase in immigration tax. Your words are reasonable and your admiration is inexplicable. However, the Dutch only know the interests and do not ask right and wrong. At first, they used our public protest in front and the national assistance behind to ease our people's anger, so they suspended the case to wait for the time. Unexpectedly, bad news came from afar that the implementation was imminent. For example, building a mountain without completing it is a heartfelt pain for overseas Chinese and the country. I humbly request that you continue to negotiate to achieve the goal of revoking the case, open a new era in Sino-Dutch diplomacy, and be the true savior of overseas Chinese in the Netherlands. Not only will the association praise you. China-Dutch Diplomatic Support Association

Various Industries Request Reduction of Business Tax 123

The Construction Industry Association previously convened various colleagues to solicit opinions on the business tax matter. It was agreed that the special circumstances of the industry, such as material substitution and labor substitution, as well as the losses due to rising material prices in recent years, should be detailed in a letter to the Municipal Chamber of Commerce for submission to the government for verification and reduction to achieve the lowest tax amount to ease the burden.

The West Clothing Industry Association Chairman and Committee Member Wang Lianfang yesterday sent a letter to the Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce and the Shanghai Municipal Industry Association Tax Regulations Research Committee stating, "Regarding the city's business tax, which is currently being studied and will be implemented soon, various industries have expressed their opinions to form good tax laws. Regarding the situation of our industry, we should contribute our views and hope for your consideration. The provisions of Article 4 of the Outline of Business Tax Collection in various provinces stipulate that luxury businesses and other businesses that should be banned should not exceed 2 per mille. This point is the most accurate standard for determining the tax rate. Those that are not luxury businesses and are not in the list of businesses that should be banned are taxed below 2 per mille to comply with the central regulations. Our Western clothing industry is the first of the four necessities of people's livelihood, and its name is not a luxury business. Its raw materials are mainly silk, cotton, hemp, wool fabrics, and woolens. In recent years, many domestic products have been invented, and their prices are several times lower than those of foreign silk and satin. Since silk and satin are not luxury businesses and are taxed at 2 per mille, the raw materials of Western clothing have no luxury business nature. As for the finished clothes, such as Zhongshan cloth and Liberty cloth, the price of each set of domestic Western clothing is only four or five yuan. If the robes and jackets of the used clothing industry are made of foreign goods or silk and satin, their prices are more expensive than Western clothing by dozens of times. This shows that the finished goods are also not luxury businesses. In particular, the form of Western clothing is stipulated in Article 4 of the National Government Clothing System Regulations, so Western clothing is not in the list of luxury businesses. It can be seen that the tax rate of 20 per mille for the Western clothing industry in Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces exceeds the central regulations. This is one point. In terms of banning, strange clothes and exotic clothes should be banned, and the form of Western clothing has been adopted by the National Government Clothing System Regulations, which is the same as the used clothing system and is a national custom clothing. However, the tax rate for the used clothing industry is 2 per mille, so why is the tax rate for the Western clothing industry 20 per mille? The same national custom clothing is manufactured by the same Chinese people and is the same manual industry. The tax rate is ten times different, which is not in line with the outline's regulations. This is the second point. According to the provisions of Article 7 of the Supplementary Measures, all kinds of businesses, regardless of whether they are engaged in local goods or foreign goods, are taxed at the same tax rate. Therefore, the Western clothing industry and the used clothing industry, regardless of whether they are manufactured for local goods or foreign goods, should be taxed together and should not be differentiated. This is the third point. Based on the three points listed above, the Western clothing industry is neither a luxury business nor should it be banned. It should comply with the regulations and be taxed below 2 per mille. Correspondingly, I request your association to forward it to the authorities so that the tax rate for the Western clothing industry is no higher than 2 per mille to show fairness and maintain the people's livelihood. I hope you will reply to my greetings."

Rickshaw Industry Association

Advocates No Further Issuance of Vehicle Numbers 124

The Shanghai Municipal Rickshaw Industry Association wrote a letter stating that since the Public Works Bureau reorganized the rickshaws in the Chinese Concession in the Republic of China in 1928, the number of vehicles in Shanghai South has been reduced from 5,064 to 4,500, and the number of vehicles in Zhabei has been reduced from 3,472 to 2,900. The North-South Vehicle Dealers Association is responsible for paying the guaranteed donation. For the past three years, the municipal government's 176th municipal meeting on the 27th of last month had a case of increasing the number of rickshaws. This quota guarantee donation system will be changed. The Shanghai Municipal Rickshaw Industry Association submitted the case to the four bureau chiefs of the Public Works Bureau, the Finance Bureau, the Social Affairs Bureau, the Public Security Bureau, and the Secretary-General for review and then reported to the meeting for a decision. They separately stated the reasons to the reviewers and requested careful deliberation, which can be divided into three points: (1) The number of vehicles should be determined based on market demand. The number of trams and public buses in the city is gradually increasing, and the rickshaw industry has been eliminated invisibly. From the actual situation, the original 7,400 vehicles should be appropriately reduced to meet the intention of promoting transportation. If the number of vehicle dealers is increased indiscriminately, the vehicle dealers will not be able to maintain their business and will inevitably affect the livelihoods of rickshaw pullers. I always remember the tragic events of the Hangzhou rickshaw puller riot on March 28, 1929, and the Beijing rickshaw puller riot on October 23. Although there is no lack of disruptive colors in this, the active promotion of public buses in Hangzhou, which seized the business of rickshaw pullers (a total of 1,000 rickshaws), and the excess of 30,000 rickshaws in Beijing were the main causes of the case. As a result, social security was affected, and rickshaw pullers suffered repeatedly. For the sake of humanity and for the sake of municipal administration, please deliberate carefully. This is one point. (2) Recently, the Ministry of Internal Affairs and the Ministry of Industry and Commerce followed the central government's orders to request the provincial and municipal governments to stipulate the maximum rental amount for rickshaws to prevent monopoly. If the quota guarantee donation system is not prevented, a monopoly will be inevitable. Only the practice of raising prices can be banned according to law, and those who are now requesting to increase the number of vehicles are not motivated by helping rickshaw pullers, but by speculative vehicle dealers who want to speculate and profit from it. The rickshaw pullers have no benefits at all. It is to sacrifice the interests of the majority for the desires of a few speculators. Please deliberate carefully. This is the second point. (3) The quota guarantee donation system for 10,000 rickshaws in the Public Concession has been in place for eight years. The price of the vehicles is several times higher than that in the Chinese Concession, and the income is less than one-third. The vehicles are being stranded every day, and there are more vehicles than drivers in spring and summer, which cannot be compensated. This is because the Public Concession has not yet been recovered, and rickshaws managed by foreigners are allowed to travel freely throughout the city. Our Chinese Concession is unreasonably restricted and cannot even provide relief. If the British note is reduced and this is increased, then the larger will be larger and the smaller will be smaller. Is it possible to plan for the gang fight? Please deliberate carefully. This is the third point.

At around 4:00 AM yesterday morning, a fire suddenly broke out at No. 68-70, Hu Min Nan Zha Road, Nanshi, downstairs of the Zhengxing Xuji Button Factory. At the time, all the workers of the factory were lodging upstairs, and everyone was in a sweet dream, completely unaware. Fortunately, Jiang Xijie, a police officer at Post No. 33 of the Second District General Office, discovered it and immediately sounded a frantic alarm while also telephoning the fire brigade. In an instant, the fire had spread. By the time the firefighters arrived in their vehicles, it had already spread to part of the adjacent No. 66, the Liyong Machinery Factory. It took about an hour of spraying water to extinguish the fire. The factory owner's wife, Zhang Wu, a native of Anhui (age 40), and the foreman, Ni Meisheng, were detained and sent to the Second District General Office. According to Wu, the fire started in the motor room downstairs, probably due to an electrical short circuit. Although there was fire insurance of 4,000 taels, it was not certain whether the insurance policy had been taken out. According to the confession, Director Wang prepared a document to be transferred to the General Bureau for verification. At 8:46 PM last night, a transformer box of the French Tram Company in Lujiawan suddenly caught fire. In an instant, the fire spread, and the sound of explosions shook the vicinity. At 11:34 AM yesterday morning, in front of the Samsung Yarn Factory on Yangshupu Road, two employees of a certain liquor store were pulling a cart that passed by. The cart was carrying four large baskets of Niuzhuang sorghum liquor. One of the employees accidentally dropped a burning incense stick into the liquor basket, and a fire suddenly started. The Yangshupu Fire Brigade rushed to the scene to put out the fire. However, sorghum liquor is extremely flammable, making it difficult to extinguish. The fire was not extinguished until after 12:00 PM. Yellow sand and other materials were used to put out the fire. However, all four baskets of liquor were burned, resulting in a loss of about 600 yuan.

Xue Die Contract Termination Case 137

Attempting Reconciliation

Through the Lawyers of Both Parties

Lin Claims Deep Regret and Eagerness to Reconcile

Hu Claims Empty Words are Useless, Treats Engagement Like Child's Play

Their Opinions are Very Far Apart

Last winter, Hu Die, a female actress of the Mingxing Film Company, received a letter from her fiancé, Lin Xuehuai, suddenly entrusting lawyer E Sen to propose the termination of their engagement. Hu, indignant at Lin's cold alliance, hired lawyer Zhan Ji to sue Lin, demanding compensation for loss of reputation and various debts. Lin also hired lawyers E Sen and Ni Zheng'ao to defend and filed a counterclaim demanding the return of the betrothal gifts, a gold bird ring. Later, Lin Xuehuai voluntarily proposed an agreement to terminate the contract and withdraw the lawsuit. However, the proposal failed to materialize due to the failure to reach an agreement. Therefore, at 9:00 AM on the 28th of last month, Zhou Renda, a judge of the Special Zone District Court, conducted the first hearing and ordered both parties to try reconciliation outside the court. If reconciliation failed, the hearing was scheduled to resume on the 20th of this month. These details have been recorded in previous reports. It is now known that Lin is very supportive of the reconciliation proposal, but Hu, because Lin's love is fickle and she fears it would be difficult to grow old together, is reluctant to fulfill the engagement. Therefore, although Lin recently entrusted lawyers E Ni to send a letter to Hu Die's representative lawyer Zhan Jifeng requesting the abandonment of previous grievances and the repair of old friendships, Zhan's reply stated that Hu required Lin to confess to the world the fabricated facts of trying to evade debts and misappropriating cars in order to seek the understanding of the world before an agreement could be reached. From this perspective, both parties are attempting to reconcile, but their opinions are very far apart. This proposal is feared to be unsuccessful, and the case will still have to be judged according to the law. The original letters of the two parties are listed below: Dear Sirs, Regarding the case of the termination of the contract between Lin and Hu, Judge Zhou of the Special Court has ordered a trial reconciliation. According to my client, Lin Xuehuai, I have never lessened my love for Ms. Hu Die from beginning to end. Because Ms. Hu's words were decisive in breaking up and asking people to dissolve the marriage contract, I wrote a letter on November 28 in a fit of anger. Now I deeply regret my recklessness and am eager to follow Judge Zhou's advice to reconcile with Ms. Hu and prove our previous alliance. Please convey my intentions to the opposing lawyer on behalf of my esteemed lawyers and ask for Ms. Hu's consent. Accordingly, I am sending you this letter and hope that your esteemed lawyers will earnestly enlighten your client with the aim of settling the matter so that this marriage contract can still be maintained. Yours sincerely, Lawyers E Sen Ni Zheng'ao, March 10, 20th year. Dear Sirs, I received your letter of the 10th of this month from your esteemed lawyers E Sen Ni Zheng'ao representing Lin Xuehuai to Ms. Hu Die requesting reconciliation and maintenance of the marriage contract, and then submitted it to Ms. Hu for review. According to the statement, the clause in the letter stating that "Die first decisively broke up and asked people to dissolve the marriage contract" is entirely a fabricated fact. The facts are there, and empty words are useless. The good intentions of Judge Zhou's persuasion for reconciliation should be respected. However, Judge Zhou's original intention in advising reconciliation was definitely not to advise temporary reconciliation, but to seek a harmonious and permanent marriage and resolve disputes thoroughly in order to achieve the purpose of reconciliation. If this purpose is to be achieved, it is necessary for both parties to be honest in their words and deeds and to have high moral character. If a person borrows money and tries to evade it, misappropriates money, fabricates rumors in anger, repeatedly seeks to terminate the contract, and suddenly rejoices and regrets their recklessness, begging to continue the old alliance, disregarding shame and treating the engagement as child's play, how can one ask what kind of happiness and results the couple will have in the future if they marry someone with such words, deeds, and character? Die is not smart, so please teach me how to deal with it. In Die's opinion, if Mr. Lin is being judged by his conscience and has made up his mind to repent, he should immediately inform society and confess the situation of fabricating facts, trying to evade debts, and misappropriating cars in order to seek the understanding of the world. In the minds of the general public, some people may criticize Mr. Lin for his moral bankruptcy. However, retreating one step is still better than those who persist in doing evil. If he does not plan to do this and only makes excuses and thinks of going back and forth, let alone speaking of reconciliation, I am afraid that the situation and the law will not allow it. Ms. Hu has entrusted me with the task of replying. I believe that the words of my client are sincere and without any falsehood. Please earnestly advise your client, Mr. Lin Xuehuai, to quickly confess the facts of whitewashing and covering up mistakes in accordance with Ms. Hu's advice in order to quell Ms. Hu's anger. At that time, I may take the opportunity to speak. I am sending you this reply and hope that you will take it into consideration and forward it to me. Sincerely, Lawyers Zhan Jifeng, Republic of China, March 14, 20th year.

Stone Lime Kiln Collapse

Crushing a Young Worker to Death 139

One Death and Three Injuries In the Tonghe Yong Stone Lime Kiln in Xiaoshadu Stone Lime Kiln, Shanghai West, business has been fairly good in recent years. However, the kiln has been in disrepair for years and is in a state of disrepair. At around 3:00 AM yesterday morning, the kiln was burning lime, and seven or eight workers were working beside the kiln when a wall of the kiln suddenly collapsed. Although the workers immediately ran to avoid it, a worker named Yang Defu was unable to escape and was crushed inside, dying instantly. Three other workers suffered minor injuries to their hands and feet. Fortunately, none were life-threatening. When the factory staff heard the sound and knew that something bad had happened, they rushed to the rescue, but it was too late. Yang Chen, the wife of the deceased, was extremely saddened by the tragic death of her husband and immediately filed a complaint with the Sixth District Police Station. The police were dispatched to bring the factory staff member Hu Yunfang to the case. District Chief Ren questioned Yang Chen, who stated that she was 30 years old, from Baoying, and currently lived in a shack in the stone lime kiln area. Her husband, Yang Defu, was 32 years old and had been working as a worker in the factory for several months. There were several children in the family, all of whom depended on her husband to make a living. Now, because the kiln was in disrepair for many years, her husband was tragically killed, and their future livelihood was insecure. She requested justice. According to Hu Yunfang, 28 years old, from Shaoxing, who worked as a staff member in the kiln, it was true that the worker Yang Defu was crushed to death by the collapsed kiln. After District Chief Ren obtained the confession, he believed that the case involved injury and death and should be prepared in writing and transferred to the District Court for interrogation.

Forensic Examination Confirms 140

Xie Changhai and Zhou Cailiang

Both Had Significant Relationships

Zhou Jindi, a 28-year-old woman from Danyang, lived in the Yufeng Yarn Factory's workshop on Pingliang Road. On January 30th of this year, at 7:00 PM, when she went to the factory to work the night shift, she was lured away and drugged, resulting in rape. She also lost a gold ring and a wool sweater. Shen Yuzhou, a Chinese detective of the Yangshupu Police Station, arrested Xie Changhai, a Jiangbei man, and sent him to the Special Zone District Court for questioning. The court ordered a forensic examination to determine whether she was a virgin and what disease she was suffering from for further verification. Shen, the detective in charge of the case, subsequently arrested Liu Peide, a suspect from Shandong Province, and sent him to the Third Criminal Division of the Special Court yesterday morning. Judge Xiao Xiefen took the seat to hear the case. The police lawyer stated the case, and the plaintiff, Zhou Jindi, stated that she had gone to the factory to work that night and forgot to bring her food basket. On the way back, she met the defendant Xie Changhai and Zhou Cailiang, who was at large, who lured her to a certain place and slept with Xie and Zhou for two nights. On the third night, she slept with Zhou, and Xie took the gold ring and sweater she was wearing. While speaking, she also cursed angrily but did not recognize Liu Peide. Zhang Hongcai, Zhou's grandfather, stated that Liu Peide was not involved. The defendant Xie Changhai was questioned and denied the abduction and rape, saying that he and Zhou Cailiang helped to look for her after she disappeared. He hesitated in his answer. Liu Peide stated that after Zhang Hongcai lost his daughter, he negotiated with Xie Changhai, Zhou Cailiang, and a certain Xing, and Zhou asked him to mediate, willing to pay 60 yuan to compensate for the loss of property. Because Zhang refused, the matter was dropped. He knew nothing about the abduction and asked for a review. The police lawyer stated that the court should issue the forensic examination report on Zhou Jindi. Judge Xiao approved it and ordered a postponement of fourteen days until Zhou Jindi's mind was completely clear for further verification. The defendant Xie Changhai was remanded to custody, and Liu Peide was released on bail. The forensic examination report is listed below:

Requesting the examination of Zhou Jindi, female, 16 years old, yarn factory worker. The symptoms of the victim are as follows: (1) The hymen has no trace, only scars remain. It has been about four weeks since the internal and external vaginal areas were eroded. (2) The patient is mentally unclear. Based on the symptoms, she was strongly threatened and suffered severe fright and stimulation, resulting in this phenomenon. As for whether she was drugged, it cannot be proven because the time has passed for so long and the drug's effect has mostly disappeared. (3) It is presumed that the victim has indeed lost her virginity, but not recently. It is difficult to determine whether her mental state can return to normal because her nature is unknown. Forensic doctors Po Ligong and Deng Jingsheng

Execution of a Pirate Leader by Firing Squad 141

Gao Tingzhen

Letters to the Editor 146

Respected Editor,

Regarding your newspaper's report today about our company's "Daji" steamship accident, specifically the part where the company's statement was relayed by your reporters, there is a slight error in the final section regarding my oral account. The original text in your newspaper states: "Generally, the families of the victims are demanding compensation from the company. However, our company believes that this unexpected disaster resulted in losses of tens of thousands of [currency unit], which is truly unfortunate. Furthermore, according to the regulations decided by the Shipping Association, any company whose ships encounter fire or other disasters on the sea is not at fault. Therefore, the requests for compensation from the victims' families should be rejected and not accepted."

Upon investigation, the Shipping Association has no such regulations as previously mentioned. I only stated that providing compensation would be quite difficult, as there are no such provisions in maritime law. I inquired with the Shipping Association, and they also have no such regulations. Currently, as an emergency measure, the board of directors is requesting the Jisheng Society to handle compensation, and the board of directors will send someone to assist. There was no mention of the Shipping Association making a decision or rejecting the compensation requests from the victims' families. It is likely that the reporters misunderstood during the hasty Q&A session. I request that your newspaper kindly make a correction.

Respectfully,

Jiang Decun, Director of Data Company

March 15th

Respected Editor,

Having read your newspaper's local news item on the 11th of this month, which stated that our association member Ge Furei caused an accident while driving City Hall vehicle number 4011 near the intersection of Qiujiang Road and Gonghe Xin Road at 3:22 PM on the 10th of this month, this account is quite different from the facts. Our association has investigated and confirmed that the accident occurred because a temporary mechanical failure caused the steering mechanism to malfunction. Moreover, the road was high in the middle and low on the sides, and the vehicle was carrying many passengers. The failure of the steering mechanism caused the vehicle to tilt to the side of the road, resulting in the accident.

The driver left the North Station at Baoshan Road at 3:12 PM, heading towards Zhenru. The accident occurred at 3:22 PM, meaning the journey was only about one and a half miles, and the time taken was ten minutes. Therefore, the claim that Ge was speeding is inconsistent with the facts. As for Xiao Shuntai's apprentice, he is now moving freely, suffering only minor skin abrasions. The injury was caused by an iron frame and iron pier placed outside the iron shop. The apprentice was working outside the shop when the steering failed, the road was high in the middle and low on the sides, and the brakes could not stop the vehicle immediately. As a result, the vehicle veered to the side of the road, hitting and knocking him onto the iron pier, causing the injury. If the vehicle had crashed onto the steps, the apprentice would have been killed.

The driver has been working for the company for two years and has a good record and is very experienced, and the incident was not caused by negligence. The driver was detained by the 4th District Police Station and sent to the local court on the 13th, where he was found not guilty. Now, the employer intends to make things difficult for the driver based on your newspaper's report. Therefore, we are providing these details to request a correction.

Respectfully,

Shanghai Chinese Public Bus Workers' Union

Respected Editor,

I am writing regarding the article in your newspaper's local news section on the 13th of this month titled "Provincial Police Detain Flower-Clothed Persons, Causing Repercussions." This report is inconsistent with the facts, and I am making the following clarification:

On the 5th of this month, our district's Detective Chief Zhang Zhaoxiang reported that while leading a patrol boat to inspect suspicious vessels, he found a cotton boat belonging to Lu A'gen on the Yunzao River. Upon inspection, the delivery note stated 150 bales of cotton from the Hengxing Cotton Mill, but this did not match the black "Tai" character stamped on the bales. It was claimed that the cotton was collected piecemeal by Zhang Jisheng of the Hengxing Mill in Yangjing Town, Pudong. Upon inspecting several bales, it was confirmed that they were of various types. Although it was not known where they were collected from, it was clear that this was an illicit business dealing in stolen goods.

Our district then ordered Lu A'gen to be interrogated. He claimed to have been hired by the Hengxing Cotton Mill to transport the cotton and knew nothing else. As the case involved the purchase of stolen goods, Zhang Jisheng had committed a criminal offense. Although Lu A'gen was only transporting the goods and was suspected of involvement, both should be dealt with by the judiciary. Our district sent Lu A'gen and a sample of the cotton to the Shanghai Local Court on the 11th for investigation.

This is the true course of events, and we request that you publish a correction in your esteemed newspaper.

Respectfully,

Fourth District Division, Jiangsu Provincial River Police Team

March 14th

Respected Editor,

I have just read today's (15th) edition of your newspaper, page 16, which contains two letters from Lu Bichou, Secretary-General of the Executive Yuan, to Nie Lusheng, titled "Letter Requesting Strict Prevention of Fundraising Under False Pretenses." The letters stated that someone was falsely claiming to be Hu Chongji, Counselor of the Eighth Division Headquarters of the National Revolutionary Army, and had fabricated a letter from Secretary-General Lu to solicit funds in Shanghai for the education of revolutionary orphans.

Hu Chongji is my name. Most Kuomintang comrades know my behavior. Since I began practicing law in Shanghai last winter, I have not been involved in external affairs, nor have I ever held any military position in the National Revolutionary Army. To avoid misunderstandings and protect my personal reputation, I have written to Secretary-General Lu to request a copy of the forged letter and to inquire about the identity of Hu Muzhou for the purpose of thorough investigation. I am also writing to request that you publish this letter so that the public is aware of the situation.

Respectfully,

Hu Chongji

Last Week's Gold Price Plunged by 44.7 Taels

Last week, the gold market experienced a brutal and volatile plunge, with complex and unpredictable fluctuations. Moments of several taels or even ten taels of price swings were commonplace. At times, price fluctuations exceeding twenty taels were observed, leaving participants bewildered and directionless. This was triggered by conflicting news, causing uncertainty among traders.

At the beginning of the week, the price reached a high of 746.9 taels [currency unit]. Subsequently, the market collapsed in a tumultuous manner, breaking through the 700-tael barrier. By Wednesday, the lowest price plummeted to 683.3 taels. This was attributed to the surge in both the overseas silver market and the Shanghai foreign exchange market. Although the situation seemed to ease afterward, the fluctuations remained unpredictable, with prices hovering around 700 taels.

By the end of the week, the price settled at 697.8 taels, representing a significant drop of 44.7 taels for the week. The difference between the highest and lowest prices reached a staggering 63.6 taels. The total number of large bars traded was 4,375. The price of silver surged by 1.375 [currency unit], largely due to HSBC extending the lending period by three tranches (totaling 0.75 [currency unit]). The daily exchange rate dropped by 0.0825 [currency unit]. The domestic market within banks was also very loose. Most Chinese gold businesses were selling forward contracts to cover their positions. The most relaxed rate offered by banks was 1 shilling and 4 pence. As for spot gold, a total of more than 28,000 bars were shipped to the United States by [Kii] Bank. It is rumored that gold shops in Shanghai still hold approximately 40,000 bars (all pledged as collateral), and that the April gold contracts are largely short positions.

It is worth recalling that the gold price reached over 790 taels in the middle of last month, but unexpectedly plummeted by over 100 taels since then. The future remains highly uncertain. Next Monday (the 16th) marks the rollover date, and short positions are still being purchased. Currently, the exchange rate is pushing down the price by 60-70 taels to 40-50 taels. Below is a summary of the week's events:

Silk and Tea: Silk Sales Still Quiet Last Week

Last week, silk sales through the banks in this city continued to be brisk. Enquiries revealed that although the textile factories in New York, Lyon, and other places had seen a turnaround in sales, and that the telegraphed prices were also increasing, the underlying situation was still weak. As Chinese silk was expensive, even if merchants sold it, they still had to lose over 200 taels per package. In addition, exchange rates remained high. The supply of goods in the hands of Chinese merchants was insufficient, and the raw materials for factory silk were limited. With the new cocoon harvest still several months away, there was no way to continue the operation. Fortunately, only four-tenths of the silk factories in Shanghai were operating, and the dry cocoons held by the financial community could still support work. Silk merchants were passive, generally waiting for the opportune moment. Transactions remained difficult to boost. The total number of yellow and white silk transactions for the week was just over 700 packages. Of those, Indian sales revived, and coarse silk purchases were strong. Current silk exports totaled about 1,300 packages. White silk head exports were also about 1,000 packages. The supply of dry cocoons could not meet the demand, and the market became more profitable. There were also no formal market prices. The prices of Chinese silk in the overseas markets in the United States and France trended upwards. — Seafarer

▲ The 1856 British Guiana one-cent stamp is said to be one of the most valuable stamps in the world, fetching an extremely high price at a Paris auction.

▲ Britain has created a map of the ocean's contours that completely marks out the 34,000 square miles of mountain and rock basins of the Pacific Ocean, representing oceanography's first major contribution.

▲ A 14-year-old boy in East London, named James Hoskowitze, is 6 feet 1 inch tall and weighs 140 pounds, a rare record among underage children.

▲ When the Eskimos of Baffin Land face famine and food shortages, the elderly men and women willingly starve themselves to leave food for the young and strong.

▲ A pike weighing 18 pounds was caught in a lake in Essex, England. Inside its belly, an unopened bottle of lemonade, still drinkable, was found.

Zhang Huizan's Utmost Mourning 152

— Yang Hua

A letter from a friend in Hunan states that the death of the late Zhang Huizan, commander of the 18th Division, was both honorable and deeply mourned, worthy of record. Opinions on Zhang's life and posthumous reputation vary, but the consensus is, "It's difficult to please everyone, but strive to have a clear conscience." Zhang's death was fitting and will not be forgotten by history.

The letter states that Zhang was from Changsha, the capital of Hunan. During his life, he held various important positions, most notably as the head of the Hunan Provincial Police Department and concurrently the head of the Changsha Police Department. Although the position might not seem prominent compared to others, returning home in glory is a different matter. Moreover, Zhang never remained unemployed for more than three months. Thus, the term "honorable life" applies to Zhang.

After the news of Zhang's death reached Hunan, He Yunqiao (Jian) immediately proposed at a provincial affairs meeting to allocate six thousand yuan for the funeral of "the late committee member Zhang of this government" (Zhang concurrently served as a committee member of the Hunan Provincial Government) and appointed Cao Mengqi, a former subordinate of Zhang, as the director of the funeral arrangements. It is said that only Zhang's head was recovered, while his body was sculpted from sandalwood. Therefore, the obituary and condolence messages all contained the phrase "Xian Zhen returns to the origin."

Currently, Zhang's coffin is about to return to Hunan. The funeral office is hastily constructing memorial arches at various locations around the East Railway Station, showing utmost mourning. The horizontal plaques and couplets at various locations are also filled with praise. For example, the horizontal plaque at the main entrance reads "Integrity for Ten Thousand Ages," with the couplet "Sacrificing one's life for the people demonstrates great integrity for a thousand autumns." The horizontal plaque at the east gate reads "Loyal Heart and Red Blood," with the couplet "General Yan's head, Changshan's tongue, protect the rivers and mountains, and shine like the sun and stars." The horizontal plaque at the west gate reads "Noble Spirit and Heroic Light," with the couplet "Confucius said achieve benevolence, Mencius said choose righteousness, the earth is the foundation, the sky is the pillar." The horizontal plaque at the east second gate reads "Suiyang Loyalty," with the couplet "Loyalty penetrates the sun and moon, noble spirit fills the universe." The horizontal plaque at the west second gate reads "Xin Guo's Loyalty," with the couplet "Unyielding to power, what is death to discuss?" The horizontal plaque at the East Railway Station reads "Spirit Never Dies," with the couplet "Ten thousand ages of rivers and mountains retain righteousness, the winds and rains of Hunan weep for the loyal soul."

Those who died alongside Zhang include Brigade Commander Wang Jiejun, Deputy Brigade Commander Hong Hanjie, Regiment Commander Li Yuefeng, Zhu Guangrong, Acting Chief of Staff Zhou Wei, Battalion Commander Huang, and countless others. These men were all sons of Hunan. Therefore, white banners and mourning flags are seen everywhere, all to summon the souls of the dead to return.

Record of the Recent Tragedy of the "Daji" Steamer 153

— Zhi Zheng

Recently, the "Daji" steamer of the Dada Company caught fire on the Jiangyin riverfront due to sulfur, resulting in a loss of no less than hundreds of thousands [of dollars], and over a hundred passengers lost their lives. It is truly a major catastrophe in river steamer history. The Dada Steamer Company was founded by Zhang Jian, a virtuous man from Nantong. It originally had four steamers operating on the inner and outer rivers: "Dashun," "Daji," "Dade," and "Dahe." Later, with the progress of business, the smaller "Dashun" and "Daji" were discontinued and replaced with new steamers, "Daqing" and "Daji." The "Daji" steamer was particularly outstanding among the company's fleet, with the largest hull and highest speed. The company had been in business for decades without incident, except for the "Daji" steamer, which had its rapeseed oil plate broken by wind some years ago. Now it has suffered this tragic incident. The "Daji" steamer is truly "Daji" (greatly auspicious) no more. It is said that the shipowner directed the rescue efforts after the accident and nearly perished. His spirit of not avoiding danger is truly commendable.

Trivial Notes on Planting Trees in the City Center 154

— Ms. Ye Hua

Arbor Day began in the fourth year of the Republic [1915], scheduled to coincide with the Qingming Festival. Later, after the establishment of the National Government, Arbor Day was changed to the anniversary of Sun Yat-sen's death, symbolizing commemoration. Since then, Shanghai has held ceremonies for Arbor Day every year. This is the fourth year, and the scale is growing, and there is more to see and hear, so it is impossible not to record it.

▲ Staff Vying to Photograph the Boss On this day, the scene was bustling, with no fewer than a hundred cameras coming and going. No fewer than thirty tripods were being carried. The city government's staff, skilled in this area, were invited to be photographers to keep as mementos and for publication. When the photographers saw the bureau chief arriving, they were extremely nervous, aiming their lenses at the bureau chief, taking pictures from left and right, repeatedly, fearing that they would not do well. Those who didn't know the inside story asked each other who it was. In reality, the staff were taking pictures of their boss.

▲ East Palace Endures a Scare The female students' dormitory of Datong University is magnificent, known as the West Palace, and facing it remotely is Fudan University's East Palace. The names of these two palaces are celebrated in Shanghai's youth circles. The tree planting preparatory staff and receptionists arrived at the ceremony venue in the morning. The site was remote and uninhabited, and there was no way to get food, so they all ate at Fudan. Many people serving in the Public Security Bureau participated in uniform. When the "queens" of Fudan's East Palace saw a group of young people striding in, mixed with armed police officers, the situation looked ominous. Rumors of an accident spread in the palace, and people anxiously inquired. Fortunately, Jiang Baiqi, Ai Dongrong, and Dong Hua Tangdi saw Yu Kuanduan arriving and told them the truth, and the group's doubts were dispelled.

▲ Please Look at Shanghai in the Future The tree planting site is in the city center, far from Zhabei, a thousand miles away. "Silent spring scenery, desolate evening cold," seems to describe this place. However, the buds of spring are just sprouting, just as the foundation of the city center is being laid. This year's tree planting in this area is a city government policy, hoping to use this festival to awaken public attention to the construction of the city center. It is said that the mayor mentioned that the city government's building in this area will open for bidding in April, begin construction in May, lay the foundation in July, and be completed in one year. The city's prosperity and growth are immeasurable. In the future, Shanghai's prosperity will be concentrated here. Today's concessions may become like Kunshan's Qingyanggang or Hangzhou's Gongchen Bridge, recovering without being recovered.

Strange Minerals 155

— Chen Boying

My friend Wei Junxin, recently returned from Germany, said that a month ago, a mountain in western Germany yielded a mineral with a color like jade, soft and translucent. There were many of these minerals, but they varied in size, with the larger ones weighing dozens of pounds. Each was individually formed, resembling bowls, bottles, basins, drums, balls, boots, umbrellas, and hats. He tried taking the thinnest piece, about one-quarter to one-third of an inch thick, and shot it with a powerful cannon shell, but it could not be penetrated. He also took the smallest one, which resembled a bowl, and subjected it to pressure exceeding ten thousand tons, flattening it. However, as soon as it was removed from the press, it returned to its original shape without any damage. Sharp blades could not cut it, hammers could not break it, and fire could not burn it. When corrosive aqua fortis was poured on it, it did not dissolve. Neither light nor heavy hydrogen lamps could melt it. No amount of tensile force could break it. All sorts of chemical and other methods were used to dissect and destroy it, but the mineral remained unchanged. Currently, many doctors of physical chemistry in Germany are studying its original substance and regretting that they are all large pieces without thin sheets, so they cannot be made into military uniforms. Otherwise, the weapons relied upon in recent wars will all become useless. I once read in the Tang Dynasty history that during the reign of Emperor Taizong of Tang, a certain country in the Western Regions presented a jade whip, slightly green in color, which could be wrapped around a finger, and knives and saws could not harm it, and water and fire could not destroy it. At first, I suspected it was a fabrication, but now, seeing what was found in Germany, it is probably the same type, and the record in the Tang Dynasty history is not false.

Recording Two Parallel Anecdotes 156

— Yun Xun

A certain gentleman lived in Shanghai and worked at a certain accounting firm. The gentleman's paternal uncle had just returned from Zhangjiakou on leave and was staying at a certain hotel on Fourth Road. The uncle knew where his nephew lived, so he immediately telephoned the gentleman. After the gentleman finished his work, he drove to the hotel to see his uncle. The uncle and nephew were not much different in age and had been childhood friends. Now, after a long separation, they met again and shared their feelings. They were very happy. Soon, a beautiful young woman arrived, claiming to have just returned from buying cosmetics. The gentleman was surprised to see her and looked closely. The woman was certainly not his aunt. He whispered to his uncle, "Uncle, when did you get such a beautiful young star?" The uncle strongly denied it, saying that he met the lady on the way through Tianjin. Since arriving in Shanghai, she has also been staying here. The gentleman did not argue and watched. Unexpectedly, that evening, they both drank too much. Around midnight, the gentleman wanted to return home and planned to rent another room to stay in, but the uncle stopped him, saying that it was fine to share a room. The gentleman said that the uncle would sleep with the lady, he would sleep alone on the left.

A was good friends with B. Their relationship was closer than brothers. Later, A was wrongly imprisoned. A's wife wept every morning and evening, at a loss for what to do. A neighbor heard and felt sorry for her, so he told A's wife, "Why don't you seek help from your husband's friend, B?" A's wife suddenly realized. However, B was a lecher. Soon, he developed a romantic relationship with A's wife. However, A was not angry at all because B helped him and he was released from prison soon after. A considered this as repaying a debt of gratitude. One day, B rented a room in a hotel and invited A and his wife. That night, the three of them slept in the same bed. A's wife and B even embraced. A's magnanimity was truly a remarkable anecdote.

Japan to Hold Chinese Painting Exhibition 157

— Jiguan

According to the "Dongbao" newspaper, the Japanese have always attached great importance to Chinese art. This time, they have launched an unprecedented initiative to prepare for a Chinese painting exhibition, which has attracted attention from all levels of society. Here is a brief description of the information obtained, which may also be of interest to those who care about art.

▲ Masterpieces of Four Dynasties The paintings to be exhibited at the exhibition have been finalized through separate contacts by the Sino-Japanese Association and the Toyo Association with key figures in the Chinese government and famous collectors. They mainly include masterpieces from the Yuan, Ming, and Qing dynasties and creations by modern celebrities. It is said that most of them are treasures that are not easily seen by the outside world for a while.

▲ Inviting Celebrities Before the exhibition, the association also plans to invite Chinese and Japanese celebrities to participate in the grand event, and will fully facilitate all transportation. Most of the Chinese invitees are from Shanghai and Tianjin. There is also news that Puyi, Xu Shichang, Jin Yunpeng, and others will bring paintings to Japan for display.

▲ Exhibition Period Scheduled The exhibition period in Tokyo is scheduled to start on April 26 and last for 25 days. After that, it will be moved to Osaka until the exhibition is completed. Except for those whose owners are willing to sell, all the paintings will be returned to China. April and May are the peak season for cherry blossoms in Japan. In addition to appreciating art, those traveling east can also fully enjoy the mountains and rivers and appreciate the famous flowers. A grand gathering is expected to take place.

In Memory of Sun Muhang Baoqi 158

— Zhang Yilin

In the old family of the west of Zhejiang, Sun Lang was especially capable in building a family. He built his standard as the governor of Qizhou. He held the festival and often went to the Envoy. The sea and mulberry fields all changed. But he never lost his personality. I met you, a lowly person. His long beard fluttering like melon face. The ministers gathered in the garden. The officials of Yuanfeng were the compilers. The rules of Bali were all about debate. Ma Zhou belonged to the grass for Chang He, and he bowed. He burned his writing. At that time, the constitutional government was just the beginning. Ganling divided the ministry, and the violent wind rose. The army was viewed in the漳 River, and the leopard mist was hidden. He was a true prefect of Kyoto, and he boasted about his eyebrow dance. The pearl spring was surrounded by banners and flags, and the yellow crane tower moved with war drums. The banners were changed, and the flags were changed. He looked forward to the war in the Central Plains. The only thing that mattered was benefiting the country. He hated 絳灌 too much. After thanking things, he met Qing Yan, and he recognized his face in the sea of people. He often wrote to Guo Linggong, and the adults returned to the Huihe. The European wind and Asian rain suddenly thundered. The sea flew in groups, and the mountains changed. There was a letter from the head of the large pillar. He had to prevent the lone note from slandering, and he wanted to stop the plan before the seat. After leaving the fire house, he planned to hide, and each collected tears in the new pavilion. He also passed on the prophecy that he should be the right person. He said dangerous words to the Qin Emperor. He took up arms in the same room to build an army. The clouds turned and the rain covered, and the crows were lost. From then on, he became a history of mutual cutting. He had no weapon in his hand, and he was sad. One day, the beacon fire broke out in Wu Yue. The crown was no longer a monkey crown. Vinegar-soaked Cao Gong's wine was used in a jar. A few inches of glue could stop the river from becoming turbid. Otherwise, he would shake his arms and return to the empty valley. Lu Duan was not confused about the big things, and Fu Bi was especially outstanding in his later years. He was born on the same year as the Dingmao bridge. He heard that you were very ill, and he was worried about your banner. He went to the hospital in Shanghai. He heard that you were sick and went to the hospital in Shanghai to see him. Not long after, he passed away. The clouds flew up and down, and he chanted Dongye. All over the sea, he called you the leader. He thought of you and did not make a long song. The tide cried for the horse of Xu Jiang.

Book and Newspaper Introduction

Vanguard Weekly 159

— Mozhi

Issue 31, published by Daguang Bookstore

Vanguard Weekly is a major publication in the nationalist literary movement, and its publication period is the earliest. If we are to capture the main trend of the nationalist literary movement from a historical perspective, then we cannot but carefully discuss this content-rich and great Vanguard Weekly. It has been published to its thirty-first issue, but each issue is improving, so that nationalist literary works are gradually becoming sound and becoming the most powerful type of literary work in modern times. None of the articles, novels, poems, and essays in this publication are not worth reading again and again. The content of this recently published issue is even more substantial, including Tang Bingruo's "Nationalist Essays," Yansu's "One Day," Ruoji's "Never Return," Xiao Jia's "Occasional Thoughts," and Zhengbo's translation of "Two Orphans" (continued), etc.

Although we have not been able to get a complete picture of Nationalist Essays, reading the first section, "The Meaning of Nationalist Essays," can make us understand the essence of this type of essay. For example, the author argues:

The emergence of nationalist essays is not as simple as commonly seen, such as sitting in an easy chair around a warm stove in the cold winter, or sipping fragrant tea in a bathrobe on a hot summer day, casually chatting with friends and moving this description onto the newspaper. Of course, this can also be said to be an essay. Others embrace singing girls in magnificent, exotic foreign houses, and arbitrarily write some short articles scolding the current society when the passion reaches its peak. This can be said to be an essay, but it belongs to slogans and has no real life. As for nationalist essays, they contain epigrams and pathos. In a short article with a central consciousness and upward direction, it can awaken the昏瞶 youth, encourage the revolutionary impulse to break through the front line of the烽火连天, fight for the rise and fall of the entire nation, and arouse indignation at the blatant imperialism's aggression against our country. Therefore, its topics, the great affairs of the world and the country, go without saying, as well as the trivial matters of the market, book reviews, news of acquaintances, feelings of wild scenery, scenes on the battlefield, the relics of the martyrs, the correction of ugliness, and one's own past that is worth recalling. As long as it is rich in the central idea of nationalism, this type of article belongs to the upward, progressive, and powerful works of nationalism.

The author's concise narrative can not only make us understand what a nationalist essay is roughly, but also indicates how we should choose materials for this type of essay. The points discussed in the first section, "The Value of Nationalist Essays," are even more distinct, acute and original. Because the full text is not finished, it will not be discussed in detail here for the time being. However, the image we get at the beginning of this article is so perfect and profound that it shows the precision of the argument in this article.

"One Day" is a short story in the form of a letter, writing about the emotions of an oppressed Annamite man who is trying to carry out a national revolution in a foreign land. The performance is so moving and powerful. After reading this article, we, the oppressed nations, not only sympathize with the suffering and misfortune of the small and weak nations, but also arouse the determination to work for the entire small and weak nations. This is the great value of this article, which has the central point of nationalist literature. For example:

...Although we have failed, our spirit will still not be depressed. At least this chills the hearts of the French imperialists.

I am already a prisoner. Prison is the hometown of revolutionaries. I feel unparalleled glory here. I am tasting the taste that revolutionaries are used to.

The day before yesterday was the day we had scheduled. At 11 o'clock at night, we raised the high flag of Annamite independence. A large team sang revolutionary songs and fiercely attacked the base camp that ruled us. We originally had only a few hundred people, but more than a thousand people temporarily joined from the people. After a fierce battle, we failed because we lacked ammunition.

That respectable female comrade was killed by the enemy in the hail of bullets. Because of her heroic influence, everyone worked harder to move forward. More than a hundred people continued to sacrifice. By noon yesterday, those who were killed, injured, and arrested had been sentenced to each of our fates. However, few people escaped.

Because my right leg was hit and I fell to the ground, I was carried here like a pig yesterday. There are already many comrades here. The narrow room is crowded with many people. The air is extremely turbid. There are sentries patrolling outside, prohibiting prisoners from speaking occasionally.

I heard that the trial will begin tomorrow. Naturally, we are prepared for the death penalty.

I bribed a guard so that this letter could be sent out... (Third letter)

This kind of courageous revolutionary will and spirit for the small and weak nations is really worthy of our admiration. Of course, it can encourage readers to sacrifice themselves forward. Because the creation in the form of letters is easy to express. Since it has true emotions, it can be written arbitrarily in the text. It does not need beautiful words to embellish it at all, so its own is a type of literary work that is easy to touch readers. It goes without saying that our inner heart is deeply moved by it, and this is even more worthy of our attention because it has the central idea of nationalism, leading us to the correct path of struggling for small and weak nations.

The poem "Never Return" is a powerful work, a truly nationalistic poem. Each poem is full of heat and power, both heroic and impassioned, and is worth singing again and again. In terms of artistic skill, it surpasses many so-called slogan-type poems. The artistic conditions it possesses can be seen in the poem "Never Return":

From today onwards, we swear never to return

Whipping and chasing the fleeing enemy

Although the warhorses are exhausted and hoarse

Although the brothers are lying on the decaying grass in the sunset

Chase to his last position

There, rescue our slaughtered brothers

We fight for freedom

We kill the enemy for our brothers

The author's performance is so skillful and powerful. In short, we are able to get such substantial and great words on a not-very-large Vanguard Weekly, which is really gratifying. In the future, I believe that there will be even more profound and powerful words presented to our readers here.

Grassland Creative Special Issue 160

— Xiao Tian

Combined Issue 11

Chinese pure literary publications are either declining or falling apart in the current state. Those that embrace the aim of promoting culture and striving to create new literature are rare nowadays. Especially those that instill correct ideas in readers with a pure attitude. Among Chinese pure literary periodicals, we have to recommend this "Grassland" weekly, which already has a considerable history.

Who is also saying that Grassland is a rare flower that has emerged in the barren Chinese literary garden, and it is the crystallization of the hard work of young gardeners. Therefore, the words in it are mostly full of upward youthfulness, as fresh as a spring night, as unrestrained as flowing water, and as majestic as a mountain peak. These kinds of works are really hard to see in other so-called big publications. At the same time, it also has the correct ideological direction, indicating a path that should be taken in literature. Because not long ago, the Chinese ideological world was really too chaotic. The publications placed before young people were either romantic or classical, either decadent or proletarian, especially this last kind of so-called proletarian literature, which instilled so many promising young people onto a deformed path. Although this kind of literary reading material that promotes incorrect ideas is flourishing, it is actually promoting the decline of Chinese new literature. If we want to save this only crisis in the Chinese literary world, we can only hope that the domestic publishing industry will produce more literary works with correct meaning in the near future. Then this Grassland Weekly author believes is one of the reading materials needed by modern young people. Moreover, its content has new improvements every time, whether it is poetry, novels, essays, etc., all the words are worth reading. This time, the creative special issue it published, each selected work has its great characteristics and can represent the unique style of each author. The exquisiteness of the words is of course unnecessary to describe, but the style of one or two articles creates a new format that is only seen in the Chinese creative world.

In addition to literary news, this issue includes the full-length creations "Diary of a Korean Girl" by Tang Zengyang, "Violet Description" by Zou Fang, "Defeat of Bad Luck" by Huang Huanruo, "Smile in a Dream" by Bai Xue, "Heart Shadow After Reunion" by Zhang Wei, and "Looking Forward to You" by Wang Tiehua, etc. Although the number of articles is not large, each one has a new style and is worth reading.

Tang Zengyang's "Diary of a Korean Girl" is a revolutionary literary work that uses a Korean woman's struggle for her nation as the center of the facts. Although it adopts the diary format, what it writes is not clichéd, but has a new style. The depiction of the woman's psychology is especially unique to the author's artistic skills. Now I excerpt a shorter one-day article from this girl's diary so that readers can understand how fluent the literature is and how rich the emotions are, and at the same time it is full of upward consciousness, such as

March 3rd

I'm always too lazy to get out of bed because I have a class at ten o'clock this morning, so around half past nine, I had to muster the revolutionary spirit that young women should have and jumped out of bed. After washing up, just as the class bell rang, I followed the red and green young female classmates to class. The professor who taught this class was Mr. Fan. His lectures on political science were really eloquent. Every word sympathized with the revolution of small and weak nations. There were many unique and correct insights that could be used as a reference for the Korean revolution, so I recorded it in detail in my notebook. I had nothing to do in the afternoon, so I translated a novel by an American master. I felt very satisfied and prepared to publish it in a magazine. Although my Japanese is better than my English, I am unwilling to translate the works of the Japanese imperialists who oppress small and weak nations, no matter whether they write about sympathy for the restoration of Korea or encourage their oppression of Korea.

I feel that the prosperity of Korea only hopes that our general female revolutionaries can work hard in China and unite with China and other so-called small and weak nations. Because Korea is already a country that has perished, it is really not easy to revive it from the heavy pressure of Japanese imperialism and get rid of their shackles by its own strength. Therefore, we unite with small and weak nations and fight on the same front, perhaps seeing a glimmer of hope. When the great Korean banner is high above our heads, I wish it in advance.

This kind of text that is easy for ordinary people to read, so-called "popularized", is most needed at present because of its production, but it already has the beauty of artistic value.

Zou Fang's "Violet Description" has a new creative style. The meticulousness of the words is like singing a beautiful prose poem for us. At the same time, it also has an upward consciousness. Such a portrayal cannot be achieved without superb artistic skills. It depicts two young people wandering in a mysterious street and finally gaining a sense of awakening, still retaining the most precious spring of young people. This is such a meaningful meaning that it is really rare in literary works. "Defeat of Bad Luck" We can understand from the name that it is an upward revolutionary work. We have read many of Huang Huanruo's creations in this publication, but I think this is a more satisfying masterpiece. He describes a woman who gave birth to a boy fighting against all evil forces. Of course, she can be victorious. The more he writes to the end, the more fully the upward spirit is expressed. As he said, "But even if the manipulation of fate makes us jump into the vast sea of people, we will definitely be able to defeat the devil-like fate by relying on our own strength. That is our song of triumph that can be played loudly. Our respective environments are bright and happy. Finally, we should work hard to obtain this kind of victory ourselves and not try to help others. And we must recognize the direction of our efforts and not run on the wrong path because of temporary indignation." These are such sincere and meaningful words that young people should listen to, right?

"Looking Forward to You" is a long sequel by Wang Tiehua. Although it is still unfinished, the more we read it, the more we feel its unique brilliance. Of course, the compactness of the structure is also the only important thing in creation. Those who read Wang Jun's "Looking Forward to You" can always understand that it is not only a powerful success in structure, but also a work of artistic value. We are unexpectedly happy to be able to read such a mature long masterpiece on a small piece of Grassland.

Of course, the other two articles are also worth reading. It is a pity that we could not see the whole picture of Zhang Wei's "Heart Shadow After Reunion" quickly. However, I always feel that it is worth unexpectedly praising that the words in this creative special issue can achieve such results and meet us on a small piece of Grassland Weekly.

Finally, the "Editor's Talk" has predicted that the poetry special issue and the criticism special issue will be published soon. I think there will be more satisfactory results because there are the most authors and poets in it. But the so-called poets here are of course those who have the cultivation and skills. We are waiting to read his more great works!

Guidelines for Book and Newspaper Introduction Manuscripts 161

(1) The text is limited to introducing the latest domestic and foreign publications. In addition to literary works, all political, economic, legal, scientific, educational, and other books and newspapers are included in the introduction. However, books and newspapers without contact will not be introduced.

(2) Pictures are limited to the latest works of new domestic and foreign artists and attached pictures related to the text.

Shanghai Market

Business News 162

▲ The Sino-Foreign Xin Xin Company on Nanjing Road announced that the company's Chinese and Western shoe department moved to the second floor last week and is operating as usual. All Chinese and Western boots and shoes and other accessories are specially discounted to benefit customers. In addition, rubber galoshes and woven satin rubber-soled slippers are especially discounted. Each pair is only sold for fifty cents to seventy-five cents, etc.

▲ The New China Restaurant at the intersection of Taitingli, Zhonghua Road, outside the Old West Gate, announced that the restaurant has Chinese and Western dishes, elegant layout, thoughtful service, potted plants and flowers, beautiful decoration, clean and spacious seats, and a hall for weddings, funerals, and celebrations. The prices are cheap, and the dishes, tea, noodles, snacks, etc. are delicious and praised by people from all walks of life. The restaurant has recently added excellent chefs to cook various dishes and snacks, so the store is unusually crowded with diners and has a hard time keeping up.

▲ The Lao Hu Kaiwen Guanghu clan pen and ink shop at the north end of the ball-throwing field announced that the shop has been opened in Shanghai for many years, and the pens and inks produced are carefully made and have long been praised as top-quality by Chinese and foreign scholars. The owner has also set up a factory in Helixi, Ningguo, to make his own coal smoke, which is unmatched by other families. Since the start of schools, the shop's business has been very prosperous and has a hard time keeping up.

Theater News 163

▲ The Baixing Grand Theater at the intersection of Old Bazi Road and Fusheng Road announced that the hospital yesterday began showing the only domestic giant film "Love Mandarin Ducks" (also known as "The Brother Who Eloped"), which is a fine production of the Lianhua Film Company, starring Wang Cilong, Tang Tianxiu, etc., and produced by Mr. Luo Mingyou. The plot is tight and the performance is realistic. It is even more exciting than the previous "Spring Dream in the Old Capital" and "Wild Grass and Leisure Flowers". It is truly a fresh force in the revival of domestic giant films. It will be shown continuously in the hospital for four days without increasing the price. It is only sold for thirty cents.

▲ Tianyi Film Company announced that the Qianlong Tour to the South of the Yangtze River film produced by the company has long been popular. Now, the new seven episodes have more exciting content. The film uses the most popular Ji Dian monk's story in society as an interlude, which is humorous and full of fun. The exterior scenes are all shot in Hangzhou, and the peaks and shadows are pleasing to the eye. Since the day before yesterday, it has been shown in the Central Cinema on Sixth Road, and the day and night shows are unusually crowded, which shows the value of the film.

▲ Jimi Dance School announced that the school has been established for a long time and has excellent results. Recently, female teachers and teaching assistants have been hired to teach various latest European and American social dance techniques. The fees are low and you can learn them. Therefore, people have been flocking to the school at No. 12 Parker Road to sign up.

Publishing News 164

▲ "Principles of Education and School Administration" is one of the Xiamen University Education Institute Series. It was recently published by the Commercial Press. The author is educator Dr. Du Zuozhou, who spent several years of hard work writing this book based on Chinese and Western learning theories. It is divided into two parts, education administration and school administration and organization, consisting of twenty chapters with sixty-four attached charts. The whole book is 200,000 words, and it emphasizes both theory and practice. It is truly a masterpiece of education in our country. Those who are engaged in national education, local education, or primary and secondary school education need to refer to it. It is especially suitable for universities to use as a textbook.

▲ Mr. Jiang Cuoxun from Yunjian is a talented and romantic scholar with a family background. He became famous in his hometown at an early age. Since the founding of the Republic of China, he has served in Beiping. Although he is often sick, he still devoted himself to studying law in his spare time. Recently, in response to the needs of the times, he published his insights and wrote the book "Constitutional Buds", which elaborates on the essence of the Three Principles of the People and the Five-Power Constitution. It is truly a rare masterpiece in recent years. It is said that it has been published and will be shipped to Shanghai for distribution in the near future. When the National Assembly is about to open, it should be read by everyone.
